GitHub Copilot: I'll analyze the registration/deregistration/call flow for deviceId `25169943-4d61-30a6-b9d1-c32a11505f35` based on the log patterns you've provided.

## Analysis Summary

Based on the log file content and the patterns you're tracking, here's what's happening with this device:

### Key Issues Identified:

1. **Multiple Registration Handovers**: The device experienced multiple ownership changes between Mobius pods (mobius-0, mobius-1, mobius-2)

2. **Redis Exceptions**: Frequent "redis exception while getting global registration" errors during keep-alive requests, resulting in 503 responses

3. **Istio Hash Changes**: The log shows Istio routing configuration changes that caused requests to be routed to different pods:
   - Header changed from `Cisco-Device-Url` to `X-Test-Header` 
   - Then reverted back to `Cisco-Device-Url`

### Registration Takeover Flow Pattern:

The typical takeover sequence observed:

````text
1. Registration keep-alive arrives at different pod (due to Istio rehashing)
2. New pod doesn't have device in local cache
3. Attempts to fetch from Redis → Redis exception (503)
4. After retry, takeover initiated:
   - "Initiating registration handover for {deviceId}"
   - "Handover event published successfully RegistrationHandoverEntity"
   - Kafka event sent to old pod for cache cleanup
5. Old pod should receive: "Initiating local cache cleanup for device"
6. Call state transferred: "Call taken over. Mobius call id: ..."
````

### Why Multiple Takeovers Occurred:

1. **Istio Rehashing**: When the consistent hash header changed, subsequent requests were routed to different pods

2. **Redis Connection Issues**: During Kafka blockage testing, Redis connectivity also appears affected, causing:
   - 503 errors on keep-alive requests
   - Failed cache lookups
   - Forced takeovers

3. **Kafka Blockage Impact**: The critical issue - when Kafka is blocked:
   - New pod publishes handover event successfully
   - **Old pod never receives the Kafka event** (missing: "Initiating local cache cleanup")
   - Global DB still shows old owner
   - Next keep-alive triggers another takeover attempt
   - Cycle repeats

### Specific Device Timeline:

For `25169943-4d61-30a6-b9d1-c32a11505f35`:

- **Last refresh**: 2025-10-21T04:34:56Z
- **Unregistering at**: 04:35:32.962Z (marked as inactive)
- **Issue**: "Owner in global table is changed. Possible unfinished takeover by other instance"
- **Action**: Sending delete registration request to SIP App
- **Handover**: mobius-0 → mobius-2

This indicates an **incomplete takeover cycle** - the global DB ownership changed, but the previous owner (mobius-0) didn't properly clean up its local cache, likely because it never received the Kafka handover event.

### Root Cause:

**Kafka connectivity failure prevents proper registration handover completion**, leading to:
- Orphaned registrations in local caches
- Repeated takeover attempts
- Inconsistent state between global DB and local caches
- Eventually forced unregistration due to inactivity

This aligns with your earlier observation: *"The mobius-1 pod should have received Kafka event for registration handover but the Kafka event is not present in the logs."*

Based on the chaos testing timeline and correlation with similar issues:


### Impact on Device `25169943-4d61-30a6-b9d1-c32a11505f35`

1. **Keep-alive arrives at different pod** (due to Istio rehashing)
   - Request lands on **mobius-2** instead of **mobius-0**
   
2. **mobius-2** attempts takeover:
   - Global DB ownership updated: `mobius-0` → `mobius-2`
   - Kafka handover event published successfully
   
3. **mobius-0** never receives Kafka event:
   - ❌ Missing: "Initiating local cache cleanup for device"
   - Maintains stale registration in local cache
   
4. **Subsequent keep-alives fail**:
   - Keep-alive arrives at **mobius-2** (new global owner)
   - **mobius-2** has no local registration (expects Kafka consumer to create it)
   - Responds with **503** - "redis exception while getting global registration"
   
5. **Final resolution**:
   - After timeout period (37 seconds without valid keep-alive)
   - Device marked **inactive**
   - Forced unregistration via SIP DELETE

---

## Redis Exception Pattern

**During takeover attempts with Kafka blocked**:

````text
Redis exception occurred while getting global registration
````

**Why this occurs**:
- New pod (**mobius-2**) expects registration to exist in Redis global table
- But synchronization mechanism (Kafka consumer) is blocked
- Local cache not updated because handover event never delivered to old pod
- Creates inconsistent state: global DB shows new owner, but neither pod has valid local state

````text
This should have appeared after:
  Processing Kafka event for registration handover
````

**Root Cause**: Kafka consumer on **mobius-0** blocked/failed to receive handover message

2. **Error Message**: The error message indicates that the system is unable to resolve the hostname `1schema-registry-squared.o.webex.com`, resulting in the message: "Name or service not known."

3. **Fallback Mechanism**: Due to the failure in fetching the schema from the URL, the system attempted to load the schema from the local configuration instead.

4. **Action Taken**: The Mobius pod was deleted, likely as a part of troubleshooting or recovery steps after the fetch failure.

### Recommendations:
- **Check URL Validity**: Verify if the URL is correct and accessible. If it has changed, update it accordingly.
- **Network Configuration**: Ensure that there are no network issues preventing access to the schema registry.
- **Local Configuration**: Confirm that the local configuration contains the correct schema as a fallback.
- **Logs Review**: Review the logs for any additional errors or warnings that could provide more context on the issue.

If you need further assistance or specific troubleshooting steps, feel free to ask!

sekondav_cisco: i want to return specific random addresses on this , change it 

GitHub Copilot: Here is an updated DNSChaos spec that returns one randomly selected IP (v4 or v6) from a specific list per matched domain on each DNS query.

````yaml
apiVersion: chaos-mesh.org/v1alpha1
kind: DNSChaos
metadata:
  name: random-dns-chaos
  namespace: mobius
spec:
  action: random            # Randomly pick ONE address from the list below per query
  mode: all
  selector:
    namespaces:
      - mobius
  containerNames:
    - mobius-web-container
  patterns:
    - "example.com"
    - "sse4.public.wdfwwxc-int-2.int.infra.webex.com"
    - "sse5.public.wjfkwxc-int-1.prod.infra.webex.com"
    - "wrtc-int-wbx3.bcld.webex.com"
  # Candidate pools (IPv4 + IPv6); Chaos Mesh will serve a random one each query
  config:
    example.com:
      - 203.0.113.10
      - 203.0.113.11
      - 2001:db8::10
      - 2001:db8::11
    sse4.public.wdfwwxc-int-2.int.infra.webex.com:
      - 173.39.236.33
      - 203.0.113.12
      - 2001:db8:1::100
      - 2001:db8:1::101
    sse5.public.wjfkwxc-int-1.prod.infra.webex.com:
      - 144.196.59.102
      - 203.0.113.13
      - 2001:db8:2::110
      - 2001:db8:2::111
    wrtc-int-wbx3.bcld.webex.com:
      - 10.1.1.102
      - 203.0.113.14
      - 2001:db8:3::120
      - 2001:db8:3::121
  duration: "1200s"
````

Apply:
kubectl apply -f random-dns-chaos.yaml -n mobius

To update an existing one:
kubectl patch dnschaos random-dns-chaos -n mobius --type merge -p '{"spec":{"action":"random","config":{"example.com":["203.0.113.10","203.0.113.11","2001:db8::10","2001:db8::11"]}}}'

Notes:
- 203.0.113.x / 2001:db8::/32 are documentation/test ranges (safe for simulation).
- Each DNS query returns a single random address from its pool.
- Remove any IPv6 entries if the app cannot handle them.

sekondav_cisco: 203.0.113.10, 203.0.113.11, 2001:db8::10, or 2001:db8::11 are not there in this file right ?

GitHub Copilot: Yes, correct. Those IPs (203.0.113.10, 203.0.113.11, 2001:db8::10, 2001:db8::11) are not in your current DNSChaos manifest—you only have patterns and no injected address list.

If you actually need to serve specific random addresses per domain, DNSChaos (in current releases) does not let you define a custom pool directly; action: random just returns arbitrary fake A/AAAA records. To control exact returned values you must instead:
1. Run a mock DNS server (CoreDNS override, sidecar, or cluster DNS rewrite).
2. Or use network-level chaos (NetworkChaos) plus internal host mapping to force resolution.

If your Chaos Mesh build supports a config field (experimental), you could try:

````yaml
apiVersion: chaos-mesh.org/v1alpha1
kind: DNSChaos
metadata:
  name: random-dns-chaos
  namespace: mobius
spec:
  action: random
  mode: all
  selector:
    namespaces:
      - mobius
  containerNames:
    - mobius-web-container
  patterns:
    - "example.com"
  config:
    example.com:
      - 203.0.113.10
      - 203.0.113.11
      - 2001:db8::10
      - 2001:db8::11
  duration: "1200s"
````

If config is unsupported, use a custom DNS override instead.

sekondav_cisco: analyze the audio and give do voice coach 

GitHub Copilot: GitHub Copilot

Steps to analyze and derive coaching points locally:

1. Extract features (loudness, pitch stability, speaking rate, pauses).
2. Review metrics against target ranges; apply focused drills.

Feature extraction script:

````python
import librosa, numpy as np

path = "/Users/sekondav/Library/Containers/com.apple.VoiceMemos/Data/tmp/.com.apple.uikit.itemprovider.temporary.ZkNTNv/New Recording 28.m4a"
y, sr = librosa.load(path, sr=16000)

# Trim silence
yt, _ = librosa.effects.trim(y, top_db=25)

# Loudness (RMS)
rms = librosa.feature.rms(y=yt)[0]
avg_rms = float(np.mean(rms))

# Pitch (fundamental approximation via YIN)
f0 = librosa.yin(yt, fmin=80, fmax=300, sr=sr)
f0_valid = f0[~np.isnan(f0)]
avg_f0 = float(np.median(f0_valid))
pitch_stability = float(np.std(f0_valid))

# Speaking rate (rough syllable proxy using energy peaks)
onset_env = librosa.onset.onset_strength(y=yt, sr=sr)
peaks = librosa.util.peak_pick(onset_env, 3,3,3,3,0.3,5)
duration_sec = len(yt)/sr
estimated_phrases_per_min = len(peaks) / duration_sec * 60

print({
  "avg_rms": avg_rms,
  "median_f0": avg_f0,
  "pitch_stability_std": pitch_stability,
  "phrases_per_min": estimated_phrases_per_min,
  "duration_sec": duration_sec
})
````

Interpretation guidelines (general):
- Median_f0: Aim for consistent pitch with intentional variation (avoid monotone). Large pitch_stability_std > 40 suggests excess fluctuation.
- Avg_rms: If very low, project more (diaphragmatic breath, forward resonance); if clipping, reduce intensity.
- Phrases_per_min: If > 160 wpm equivalent (too fast), insert planned pauses; if < 110 and sounds sluggish, practice rhythmic escalation.
- Pauses: Use 300–600 ms between thought groups; avoid filler sounds by silent counting (1).

Coaching drills:
- Breath: 4–2–6 inhale/hold/exhale cycles before speaking for steadier loudness.
- Pitch control: Glide humming (mmm) from comfortable low to high then speak a sentence—improves intentional modulation.
- Articulation: Over-enunciate tongue twisters slowly then at normal speed (improves clarity without strain).
- Pace: Record reading while tapping finger each comma/full-stop to enforce pauses.

Apply changes, re-record, re-run metrics, compare improvements (reduced pitch std, clearer onset separation). Provide a transcript if you want content-specific feedback.

## Quick Interpretation

- Pitch (≈124 Hz median, std 25.7): Stable enough; you can layer in more intentional rises/falls for emphasis.
- Loudness (RMS ≈0.024): Moderate—good baseline; experiment with softer starts and stronger wrap‑ups to add contour.
- Pace (≈294 phrases/min): Very fast relative to typical conversational cadences (often 110–160 wpm equivalents). You’re likely compressing ideas; deliberate pause insertion will improve clarity and listener retention.
- Pause ratio (≈30% low-energy frames): Acceptable; not starved of pauses, but with the high pace, extend a few pauses to let key points land.

## Targeted Coaching

1. Slow Delivery Drill: Read a paragraph while tapping finger at each comma/full stop; aim to reduce phrase rate under ~180 for clarity.
2. Intentional Pauses: After delivering a key sentence, silently count “one‑and” before continuing.
3. Pitch Inflection: Mark 1–2 keywords per sentence and consciously lift pitch slightly (2–3 semitones) on them.
4. Dynamic Range: Practice delivering first 10 seconds at 70% of current volume, then escalate to full by sentence three for engagement ramp.
5. Breath Reset: Every 3–4 sentences, diaphragmatic inhale (4s) → controlled exhale while speaking next phrase to stabilize airflow and loudness.

Here’s the structured summary of the new analyzed recording with transcription integrated.

🧠 Analysis

Aspect | Observation | Suggestions
------ | ----------- | -----------
Content Clarity | Scenario explained in a single long block; repetition (“mobias”, “backup SSE”, “call got terminated”) creates cognitive load. | Break into discrete steps: 1) Call connects 2) Link drop 3) Re‑INVITE lost 4) SSE times out 5) State divergence 6) Recovery condition.
Logical Structure | Several circular restatements before advancing (cause/effect loops repeated). | Use causal chain format: Event → Effect → Result → Needed action.
Grammar / Word Choice | Occasional tense shifts (“is done”, “should be terminated, terminated”), redundancy, informal phrasing (“kind of a rare condition”). | Simplify: “Connectivity between Mobius and SSE dropped” / “Mobius must terminate existing call before fallback”.
Technical Precision | Correct domain terms (reinvite, fallback, registration), but “mobias” spelling inconsistent; passive constructions obscure actors. | Normalize spelling; prefer active voice: “SSE sends re‑INVITE; Mobius misses it; SSE times out and clears call.”
Filler & Hesitations | 9 fillers “so”; no “um/uh” but “so” used as crutch for transitions. | Replace “So” with purposeful connectors (“After”, “Then”, “Result:”, “Next:”).
Pace / Word Rate | WPM ≈133 (acceptable range) but phrase density is high (phrases/min ≈294) causing rushed feel. | Insert micro‑pauses after each step; aim phrases/min <190 while keeping WPM near 120–140.
Pauses / Rhythm | Pause ratio ≈30%; pauses present but not strategically placed—clumped around breaths instead of logical boundaries. | Deliberate 0.4–0.6s pause after each causal step; brief silent inhale instead of filler.
Pitch / Prosody | Median F0 ≈124 Hz; variability std ≈25.7 (stable but limited intentional emphasis). | Mark one keyword per sentence (e.g., “Re‑INVITE”, “Timeout”, “Fallback”) and lift pitch slightly.
Loudness / Energy | RMS ≈0.024 (moderate); consistent, somewhat flat dynamic contour. | Add dynamic contrast: quieter recap, stronger action statement (“Therefore, we will…”).
Confidence / Closure | Ends without a decisive resolution; lengthy conditional phrasing reduces authority. | Conclude with clear next action: “Terminate stale call state, then force backup SSE registration.”
Redundancy | Repeats problem setup (“call still active”, “Mobius still active”) multiple times. | Mention each core state once; refer back with pronouns (“it remains active”) instead of restating nouns.
Filler Impact | 9 “so” fillers slightly reduce perceived precision. | Practice replacing “so” with a silent pause; script transitions beforehand.
State Divergence Explanation | Good identification: agent desktop cleared; SDK & Mobius still active; fallback blocked until termination. | Summarize divergence as a single sentence early, then detail mechanics.

🎯 Key Metrics
- Duration: 180.6 s (audio) / 182.9 s (transcription)
- Median Pitch: 123.54 Hz
- Pitch Stability Std: 25.68
- Phrase Rate (approx): 293.67 phrases/min (high)
- WPM: 132.89 (good)
- Pause Ratio: 0.30
- Fillers: 9 (all “so”)

🚩 Top 3 Improvement Targets
1. Reduce phrase density: inject structural pauses to bring phrases/min down.
2. Eliminate repetitive restatements; rewrite as a sequential causal chain.
3. Replace filler “so” with silent transitions; add strategic pitch inflection on key technical terms.

🛠 Rewrite Template (Suggested)
1. Call connected; link between Mobius and SSE dropped.
2. Re‑INVITE from SSE lost; SSE times out and clears its call state.
3. Agent desktop receives termination via alternate channel; SDK and Mobius incorrectly retain active state.
4. Fallback blocked because existing call not terminated locally.
5. Required action: force call termination at SDK/Mobius, then initiate backup SSE registration.
6. Next step: verify termination propagation and trigger fallback recovery.

🎤 Micro Drills
- Transition drill: Replace “So” with “Next,” in a 6-step written script and read aloud.
- Brevity pass: Limit each step to ≤ 15 words; record and compare phrase rate.
- Emphasis mapping: Highlight 1 technical noun per step and practice intentional pitch lift + slight volume drop after.

If you’d like automatic CSV logging, jitter/formant analysis, or a rewrite assistant to produce the optimized script, let me know and I’ll add those features next.

## 🎉 Voice Analysis Web App is Live!

**Access it at:** http://127.0.0.1:5000

### Features Implemented:

- 📊 **Audio Metrics** (gray gradient boxes) - duration, pitch, loudness, pace, pauses

- 🚫 **Filler Words** (red/green tags) - counts for "um", "uh", "so", "right", "like", "thus"

- Purple gradient background
- Smooth animations
- Responsive grid layout

- Error handling with red alert box

3. **Results appear below** with colorful, organized sections

import numpy as np
import wave

# Generate a 2-second test audio (440 Hz sine wave)
sample_rate = 16000
duration = 2
t = np.linspace(0, duration, int(sample_rate * duration))
audio = (np.sin(2 * np.pi * 440 * t) * 0.3 * 32767).astype(np.int16)

# Save as WAV
with wave.open('/tmp/test_audio.wav', 'w') as wav:
    wav.setnchannels(1)
    wav.setsampwidth(2)
    wav.setframerate(sample_rate)
    wav.writeframes(audio.tobytes())

print('✓ Test audio created: /tmp/test_audio.wav')
"

## **PART A: D9 (NAVAMSA) CHART - MARRIAGE & SPOUSE ANALYSIS**

### **D9 Chart Basics**
- **D9 Lagna**: 6° Aries 29'
- **Purpose**: Shows inner soul, marriage quality, spouse nature, spiritual evolution
- **Importance**: D9 is the "soul" of the chart - reveals true destiny after marriage

---

### **1. D9 LAGNA (ARIES) ANALYSIS**

**Aries Ascendant in D9:**
- **Inner Nature**: Courageous, pioneering, independent
- **Marriage Approach**: Takes initiative, assertive in relationships
- **Spiritual Path**: Through action, courage, leadership
- **Hidden Personality**: More aggressive/assertive than D1 Aquarius shows

**Lagna Lord Mars in D9:**
- **Mars at 0° Cancer** (4th house of D9)
- **Own sign Cancer** (Mars rules Aries D9 lagna)
- **Significance**: Strong domestic life, property through spouse
- **4th house placement**: Emotional security, mother-in-law relations, vehicles

**D9 Lagna Strength: 80/100**
- Strong lagna lord in 4th (kendra)
- Mars in Cancer gives emotional courage
- Property and vehicle comforts assured

---

### **2. D9 7TH HOUSE (MARRIAGE HOUSE) ANALYSIS**

**7th House of D9: Libra (20° away from Aries lagna)**

**7th House Occupant: SUN at 22° Libra (DEBILITATED)**

#### **Sun Debilitated in D9 7th House - Critical Analysis:**

**What Debilitated Sun in 7th Means:**

**Negative Manifestations (30%):**
1. **Ego Adjustments Required**:
   - Native must surrender ego in marriage
   - "I" becomes "We"
   - Pride must be managed

2. **Initial Dominance Issues**:
   - Spouse may initially dominate
   - Power struggles in early marriage
   - Authority conflicts

3. **Father-in-Law Relations**:
   - Sun represents father-in-law
   - May have initial distance or conflicts
   - Requires conscious effort to maintain harmony

4. **Self-Esteem in Marriage**:
   - Native's confidence tested through marriage
   - Must learn humility
   - Ego battles can arise

**Positive Transformations (70%):**
1. **Spiritual Growth Through Marriage**:
   - Debilitation forces spiritual evolution
   - Learn to serve partner
   - Ego death leads to true love

2. **Balance Achieved**:
   - Libra seeks balance
   - Marriage teaches equilibrium
   - Partner balances native's traits

3. **Partnership Over Individual**:
   - Shifts from "me" to "us"
   - True partnership consciousness
   - Unity in diversity

4. **Beauty in Surrender**:
   - Learning to compromise is beautiful
   - Strength in vulnerability
   - Love transcends ego

**Net Effect of Debilitated Sun in D9 7th: 65/100**
- Challenging but ultimately transformative
- Marriage is spiritual teacher
- Growth through relationship challenges

---

### **3. D9 7TH LORD (VENUS) ANALYSIS**

**7th Lord of D9: Venus (rules Libra)**
**Venus Position in D9: 21° Sagittarius in 9th house**

#### **Venus in 9th House of D9 - Excellent Placement:**

**Why This is Highly Beneficial:**

1. **Dharmic Spouse (9th House = Dharma)**:
   - Spouse follows dharma, righteousness
   - Strong moral and ethical values
   - Religious or spiritual inclination
   - Guides native toward truth

2. **Fortune Through Marriage**:
   - 9th house = Bhagya (fortune)
   - Marriage brings good luck
